Resubmission - Challenge Problem 6¶

Barbod Khaleghi

My first mistake came from the question section. The answer I provided below was not a bioinformatics method and thus not applicable to be used.

My old answer: "Googled: “protein-protein interactions bioinformatics analysis mass spectrometry biopython” Link picked: https://www.nature.com/articles/s41467-021-23666-z Crosslinking MS is a desirable method since proteins do not need to be tagged and can identify even weak interactions. Recent studies have tried to use the MS to map the protein-protein interactions (PPIs). It starts with estimating the PPI False Discovery Rates (FDRs). Error rates can be estimated using a target-decoy approach. During this approach, the number of matches to the decoy database correlates to the rate of false positives. Then, the list of protein-protein interactions is trimmed down to only the ones with desirable false discovery rates."

In learning more and using an actual bioinformatics method for protein-protein interactions analysis, I understand that PPI-MASS would be useful for this. This python webserver is a commonly used method of bioinformatics to help in the analysis of protein-protein interactions through understanding the mass spectrometry of the proteins. It is found here: https://minicad.appsbio.utalca.cl/ppi-mass/

Below, I have included all of the necessary code. The only mistake I made is on question 7F because I was unable to combine the dataframes above. I could not complete it without merging the dataframes and thus don't have old code to show for it. I will include all of the code and explain what I did different around that the 7F PCA part I messed up on.

For the part below, my computer will not allow me to run this code. It remains stuck on In[*] as it is constantly running. I tried searching for solutions but it may be due to the for loop in this code running infinitely. Either way, it was unable to be completed using my computer but below is all the correct code including how to do a PCA. First, I used the functions presented and a for loop system to combine the the data frames into one to be used for the PCA titled npx_data. This was done using the for loop method with i and j as the parameters. Next, to run the actual PCA, I used model.fit and PCA() to construct the plot. In doing so, I also set the labels of the plot using various functions to craft a clean plot. Lastly, PC1, PC2, and PC3 were each created. Using the scatter plot function, I was able to make plots comapring PC1 and PC2 as well as PC1 and PC3.

print(NPX.head())

s = pd.Series(NPX.SampleID.unique())
print(len(NPX.UniProt.unique()))

npx_data = np.empty(shape=(len(s), len(NPX.UniProt.unique())))
print(np.shape(npx_data))

y=0
for i in NPX.UniProt.unique():
    x = 0
    for j in s:
        if j in list(NPX[NPX['UniProt'] == i].SampleID):
            npx_data[x,y] = NPX[(NPX['SampleID'] == j) & (NPX['UniProt'] == i)].NPX
            print(npx_data[x,y])
        else:
            npx_data[x,y] = 0
        x+=1
    y+=1

print(npx_data)

In [ ]:
df = pd.DataFrame(npx_data, columns = NPX.UniProt.unique(), index = s)
print(df.head())
In [ ]:
model = PCA()
model.fit(df)
transformed = model.transform(df)
features = range(model.n_components_)

normalized_variance = model.explained_variance_/(model.explained_variance_.sum())
print(normalized_variance)

plt.bar(features, normalized_variance)
plt.xticks(features)
plt.ylabel('variance')
plt.xlabel('PCA feature')
plt.xlim(0,10)
plt.show()
In [ ]:
PC1 = transformed[:,0]
PC2 = transformed[:,1]
PC3 = transformed[:,2]

plt.scatter(PC1, PC2, c=df.Binary_Case_Control)
plt.ylim(-10,10)
plt.xlabel('PC1')
plt.ylabel('PC2')
plt.show()
